4.Evolve How To See Ads Performance Our Recommended
Columns
Alright, so now once you've basically set up your DCT campaign, if you were previously running
ads, you're going to want to go through and find out what your best performing ads are. So that's
what I'm going to show you how to do in this video. Now, if you were not running ads before or
you don't have any previous best performing ads, then what you're going to do is you're still going
to watch this video because I'm going to show you how to set up these columns and then
basically be able to tell what is actually performed.
So the way that we like to basically go through and do things is we only care about ads that are
getting spent and ads that are getting results. So if we have an ad that say, for example, over the
last seven days, we spent $2,600 in this account and you can see, for example, this ad right here
has gotten like $250. It's doing okay.
It's at like a 3.9. In this instance, this is not really an ad that excites me compared to an ad that is
getting the bulk of the spend like these three ads here and getting great performance. So what
we're looking at here, I know everybody wants to look at cost per click and add to carts and all
this other stuff. It doesn't matter.
What do you pay bills with? You pay bills with money. So we need to focus on where the money
is. So first thing that you're going to need to do is you need to make sure that you actually have
columns in place to see the performance.
So what you're going to do is you're going to click columns here and you go down and you're
going to click customize columns. And now this is just the stack of columns that we use. So we
have campaign.
We have date created. We have delivery. We have bid strategy.
We don't really care about bid strategy. You can actually delete that. We have attribution setting.
We have budget, amount spent, results, cost per results, purchases with all of these boxes
unticked, cost per purchase, purchase conversion value, purchase ROAS, impressions, reach,
frequency, and I'll explain all these in a second. Unique outbound click or sorry, CPMs, unique
outbound clicks, cost per unique outbound click, unique outbound CTR, add to cart, cost per add
to cart, checkouts initiated, cost per checkout initiated, engagement rate, quality ranking. You're
all parameters.
And then we'd like to add conversion rate and we'd like to add AOV and we'd like to add video
hold and video hook. Now, what you're going to want to do is first off, understand what all these
are, which I'm going to explain very shortly. But you're going to want to add every single one of
these that I just told you to your columns.

So how do you find, for example, purchases? Well, you're going to go into the search bar here
and type in purchases. Right. And as you can see, you're just going to select purchases.
Now, what will happen just so I can show you is if I select purchases, it's going to add them with
all these different basically viewpoints. So mobile and website and offline and meta just untick all
of these. OK.
And then if you want to actually move them around, I just click the little hamburger menu here
and I just drag this around like this. OK. And I like to have, again, my my column set this way.
So it's like I can see purchase. What was my cost to get it? What was the total value? What was
the return on ad spend? And that's how I kind of have these setups. You can see this here.
I'm not going to beat that down. But all these metrics you can actually look at. Another thing as
well.
And if you just type in link clicks, you can also just do unique link clicks or link clicks and CTR.
That is fine. OK.
You don't have to use outbound for the most part. They're all kind of the same. So you don't need
to be confused about that.
And to be honest, I don't even look at cost per click. I look at it at a smaller level to just kind of get
a better understanding of how the ads are doing. But for the most part, again, all that matters is
how much are we spending and how much are we making.
OK. So from there now, what you're going to do is you're also going to probably want to create
these custom metrics here. So how do you create a custom metric? Well, you click this lovely
blue button up here and you're going to create specific metrics called video hook, video hold,
conversion rate and average order value.
So if you saw AOV is purchase conversion value divided by purchases. So you're going to create
a custom metric and you're going to click inside of here. You're going to type purchase and you
should see purchase conversion value.
And you're going to click the division sign and then you're going to do purchases. And we're going
to name this average order value. We're going to make sure that this is a currency.
So obviously a dollar amount. And you can just make this everyone with access in the business
or only you. Go ahead and click create metric.
And just like that, I have now created the AOV metric. OK. And you're going to do the same thing
for conversion rate, which is purchases divided by landing page views.

Also, you can do purchases divided by link clicks. But we typically do landing page views for this.
Video hook is going to be three second video plays divided by impressions.
And then video hold is going to be through plays divided by impressions. And if you're like
Spencer, what the heck is all this? I'm going to explain this all very shortly. But these are also
going to be very helpful metrics for you to better understand what is going on.
OK. Then once you have all these selected, you're going to want to make sure. So, for example,
let me go ahead.
You saw Facebook just removed all of that. I'm going to add my video hold, my video hook, my
AOV and my conversion rate. I'm going to add those there.
And again, you can move these around however you'd like. So, for example, if I want to move my
AOV up, I can move it up here. Conversion rate, move it up.
And then I actually typically like to move my video hold up here with the link clicks and my video
hook up here with the link clicks as well. It's kind of annoying when you have to go through like
this. So, sometimes you got to drop it.
I haven't found a better way to do this. I'm sure there's a better way. But it can be kind of
annoying to organize it.
But once you organize it, you click save as a column preset. And then obviously, just make sure

dollar sign.
Then you click apply. And boom, just like that, it will now be applied. Sometimes it actually won't.
So, if you still see here, it says like custom, then just make sure you click this and actually select
the one that you want to select. Okay. So, now what we need to do is we need to figure out how
to look at performance, right? Well, let's take a look here over the last 30 days.
And this will give me a pretty good understanding of what's actually performing. So, for this client

well. We've launched one DCT, and this DCT is doing okay.

Here's an ad that obviously has done pretty well. But just make sure that you take into
consideration any ads that are older than three months or I would say six months at most. Just be
careful of them.
I would always try to look within like the last 90 to 30 days of what your best performing ads are in
regards to figuring out which ones you should use. But with that said, now that we actually have
our column set up, we can now look at the performance. So, again, we have date created.

purchase, and cost per purchase.

sometimes we will get shop orders. So, this is just a website purchase.
So, if this is not like website and shop, again, I'm not trying to confuse you there. But we just have
these double up columns here just to make sure we can keep track of total purchases, if there are
others, and then the website purchases. Okay? And then from here, I'm looking at CPA.
So, CPA is going to be one of the main ones that you want to look at. So, whatever your average
order value is, obviously, you're going to have a target CPA around that. And then, for example,
over here, we're going to have our purchase return on ad spend.
So, this is the big one that a lot of people look at. So, if you're scaling off of return on ad spend,
which majority of you probably should be because you need profitable growth in your business,
obviously, the return on ad spend is going to play a big factor for you. And then as we scroll
down, we can see impressions.
Impressions is basically the total number of people that saw your ad. And reach is the individual
people that saw your ad. So, you can see, for example, over the last 30 days that we had a 5.95
frequency in the ad account.
Which means that, on average, people saw our ad over five times, which is pretty intense for a
30-day period. And we definitely need to improve our prospecting ads here. But those are the
numbers.
So, 185,000 people were reached individually. And out of those people, they, on average, saw it
about 5.6 times. That's what frequency means.

Okay? And if you hover on this, you can see, again, the average number of times each account
center saw your ad. CPM tells you what your advertising cost is. This is definitely an important
metric to look at.
Because if your CPMs are crazy high, it's going to be really hard for you to be profitable. Right
now, we're paying about $10 to get in front of 1,000 people. And we've earned that right.
Okay? This is definitely very, very good. Depending on the account, sometimes you might have
to pay, you know, $30, $40, $50. We've seen it get as high as $60, $70.

How many clicks, how many people clicked our ads, what the cost of that was. So, for example,

Anything above a 1.5% is good, but at the end of the day, if the ad is profitable, it doesn't matter

what's going on. So, for example, this ad had almost double the cost per click, and it still had a

So, 21% is okay. 30% is good. 40% is really good.

If you have a 50% hook rate, that means every other person that sees your ad is stopping to

impressions. So, three plays are either 15 seconds of your ad.
So, if you have an ad that's 30 seconds, somebody watches at least 15 seconds. Or if you have

through play.

💥 Action Item - Launch Your Campaigns

**REMINDER:**  
We do NOT recommend purging and turning off all of your existing campaigns.

This campaign should simply be added alongside whatever campaigns you already have and be your NEW campaign for testing and scaling.

A your other campaigns begin to die out over a few weeks or months, then you can begin to optimize them and turn them off.

👣 Evolve

22%

🎁 Bonuses

💥 Action Item: Take a Breather

### Time To Take "Inaction" lol

Listen, that module that you just watched was dense as hell.

You just consumed a shitload of information.

So, what I want you to do is take a breather.

Go touch some grass

Go have some lunch, eat some dinner

Whatever you need to do.

However, if you did split up that module into multiple sessions, that's fine

But, what's really important for you to do now (or once you get back) is to open up a Google Document or a note page and write down your 3-5 biggest takeaways so they STICK:

**Examples:**

1. The broader my avatar, the better everything else has to be.
2. Desires are great for creating core avatars.
3. Etc.

Once you've written your takeaways, it's time to proceed to the next session, where we start to build out the avatars together.

ps. If you watched the ENTIRE lesson in 1 day, come back to the next module tomorrow or later today.

BESTAND: 1.1 Evolve _ Facebook Ads Strategy Philosophy.mp4

All right, in this video, we are going to be covering our strategy from a high level so you can actually better understand the philosophy behind this before you think, what is this? Okay? I have tried every single, why, that's a lie. I have tried almost every single ad structure and media buying strategy that's out there. Okay? I can confidently say that this is probably the best and it is the easiest structure to run. Okay? So, the campaign level, we will talk more about this as we get deeper into it, but I just want to give you a high level overview here. We run one campaign. It is called the Acquisition Campaign and it is fully broad. Okay? It does retargeting for you, it does prospecting for you, it does middle of funnel for you, it does everything for you. Okay? You do not have to have separate campaigns and you do not have to have a testing campaign or a scaling campaign or an audience this or audience that. Audiences don't matter. Okay? This is broad. We are going broad and again, I will explain this further as we get deeper into it and all you are doing at the campaign level is you are controlling the budget. Okay? You are going to say, this is my budget Facebook, here it is and I want you to spend it because you are my friend and I trust you. Okay? Very rich friend, but you trust him. The next thing is that by having it in one campaign, we have a scalable environment and a scalable environment means that when we test ads, we are testing ads in the arena. Okay? We are not, you know, starting it, we are not starting these ads on the playground. Okay? We are throwing them right in the coliseum. They are getting after it. Okay? They are going to face the best of the best. There is no warm up. There is no, oh, let me just test a little bit of spend here. No. We are going to put them in the one scalable environment that we have to see if they are worthy of getting spent. Okay? So, the reason this was the big breakthrough for me and this is what makes this strategy so powerful is we do not have to waste spend. Okay? If an ad gets spent in this campaign, in this structure, that means that you, nine times out of ten, have found a new winning ad and that also means that it is a good ad. It is going to perform better than all of the other ads that you have inside of here. Okay? If a spend, or if a spend, if an ad does not get spent, it is a bad ad. And this is probably the hardest thing for people to understand. And I am telling you, we hire new media buyers probably every couple of months and when they see this strategy, it kills them. And I am not going to lie, it killed me too for the longest time. And I seriously, for six months, would take any ads that did not get spent and I would take them out of there and I would put them in an ABO campaign. If you do not know an ABO campaign, basically it is where you can force spend on ads rather than letting Facebook choose where to spend. But I would take any of these ads in this campaign that did not get spent and say, you know what Facebook, I am smarter than you and I would put it in an ABO campaign and I would force $25, $50, $100 a day on it and I would let it spend. And what would you know? It would not work. It would get a 0.5 extra turn on ad spend. Meanwhile, this campaign was absolutely ripping and getting a 3, 4X. And then I do it again. I do it again the next week. I am like, okay, well, this ad, this ad, obviously Facebook did not read it properly. I know this ad is going to do the same thing. I would spend on it, spend $300, $400, it would not convert, turn it off. Same thing again, a month later, I was like, okay, no, no, I know Facebook is not smarter than me. I am going to take this ad, these new images that we did, there is no way that these are not good enough to scale. So I am going to take them out and I am going to force spend on them. And would you guess that same thing happened. The performance was terrible. I have not seen an ad in one of these DCT campaigns that did not get spent. I have not seen us take it out, spend on it, which we have probably tested about 60, 70 ads at this point. I have not seen a single one of these ads that did not get spent in this campaign outperform in a separate campaign. It has not happened. And if it does, if it does perform, it performs for maybe three or four days and then it falls off the face of the earth and it absolutely crumbles. So this campaign is saving you money and actually optimizing your performance. As you could tell, I am very passionate about this because I have been slapped in the face by Facebook so many times. So I understand you are probably going to have your perceptions on this of like, this does not seem right. This does not, you know, I just want to retarget. I want to do this. Okay, listen, if you want to go ahead. But I am telling you, this is the best strategy that you can use. And I am saying that confidently because I have seen us spend $40,000 on a single campaign and I have seen it absolutely crush. $40,000 in a day. This is showing $50,000 in a month. We were spending $40,000 a day in a single campaign. This strategy works. The other thing that you need to know is our 3-2-2 testing method. And the reason why we do this is because rather than us actually putting, you know, three different ads in there, what we actually do is we give Facebook the ability again to choose them for us. All right, Facebook, here's three images around this one concept, which is kids images. Okay, that was our idea. And we got three different images of kids and we tested them with two pieces of copy and two pieces of headlines, all right, so headline copy. And we let Facebook choose. How To See Ads Performance + Our Columns

17:10

**Our Columns:**

- Campaign
- Date created
- Attribution setting
- Delivery
- Budget
- Amount spent
- Results
- Cost per result
- Purchases
- Cost per purchase
- Purchases conversion value
- Purchase ROAS (return on ad spend)
- AOV
- CVR
- Impressions
- Reach
- Frequency
- CPM (cost per 1,000 impressions)
- Link clicks
- Cost per link click
- Link CTR (click-through rate)
- Video Hook
- Video Hold
- Video average play time
- Adds to cart
- Cost per add to cart
- Checkouts Initiated
- Cost per checkout initiated
- URL parameters

🆕 Understanding Ad Definitions

16:25

**Ad Definitions:**

Please note that the definitions that follow are the ones we have chosen to use.  
  
At the end of the day, I want you to use the definitions that make the most amount of sense to you.

But hopefully these help guide you so we can think less about terms and philosophies and just focus on pure execution.

**💻3:2:2** ⇒ 3 creatives, 2 body copies, and 2 headlines  
**12-Year-Old Definition:** The testing structure we use inside of Meta.  
**Example:**  
*This ENTIRE thing is a Concept. “3” = Variations of that 1 Concept.  
“2:2” = 2 Headline + 2 Body copy for that Concept that you put inside of Meta.*  
  
📂 **Concept/Batch/Test #:**⇒ The tracking number for this test

**12-Year-Old Definition:** The number you use to keep track of which test you're on

**Examples:**  
*Batch #1, Batch #29, Batch #133  
*  

**💡Concept/Swing** ⇒ The test strategy - what you're testing in this batch

**12-Year-Old Concept Definition:** The big idea behind the ads you want to test

**Examples:***  
"Test an iteration on a winning video."*

*"Test superlative angles."*

*"Test UGC format"*

*"Test different avatars."*  

**🔗Angle** ⇒The selling strategy - how you're choosing to sell the product

**12-Year-Old Angle Definition:** The main reason you're giving someone to buy  
  
**Examples:**  
*"Your child will enjoy taking their greens" - Grüns*

*"It will help your digestive system" - Grüns*

*"You won't be drinking microplastics" - Liquid Death*

*"You'll look cool while you drink us" - Liquid Death*

*Key insight: Every ad needs an angle. Even if your concept is "testing formats," you still need to define what you're selling. If your concept is “Testing X Angle” the concept becomes the angle. But for tracking purposes, I prefer to actually JOT DOWN the angle twice so we can be sure.  
*

**🔀Variations** ⇒ Individual executions of the angle(s)  
**12-Year-Old Variations Definition:** Different ways to communicate your selling reason(s)

**Example:***  
If your angle is "Buy It For Life," variations might be: "One harness, lifetime of adventures," "Buy it once, adventure for life," or "End the replacement cycle"*

*If testing multiple angles, variations might be different angles like "Stainless steel," "Doctor-designed," "Easiest to clean."  
  
*🖼️ **Format** ⇒ How you deliver the ad

**12-Year-Old Format Definition:** The type of ad you're making

*Example: You could show the same message as a video of a real person talking, a slideshow of pictures, or just a product image.*

<audio><source type="audio/mpeg"></audio>

But until we actually understood what makes people tick, again, what identities they want to resonate with, whether or not they actually believe us, the desires that they have, their awareness levels, how sophisticated the market is, these five core things have really, really transformed the way that we advertise. But I promise if you just stick with it, if you circle back on these and you dive deeper and listen to some of the recommendations that I provide, you will definitely be far ahead of a lot of other marketers and you will actually have a huge advantage in your market.

Okay, so let's go ahead and let's dive in. So what is desire? Okay, let's go ahead and define this because obviously it's very important to define it but basically desire is the force that makes advertising work. You cannot create desire, okay? It is something that just exists in the market. And desires, as you can see here, are defined as strong feelings of wants or needs or wishes. It's related to, as that sentence explains, basically what people want. What is it that people actually want? We have sometimes referred to desire as the angle behind your ad. So if you've heard, hey, what's the angle of this ad? Desire is very, very similar to that but angle is more of like an umbrella. We'll get to that. But just know that two most important things here, desires are the things that people want, the things that people need, okay? And it's demand that already exists and is flowing through the market. You cannot create desire, you cannot make massive millions amounts of people want a certain thing. That desire just has to be there, okay? So types of desire in the market. Now there are basically two main types of desire that exist, okay? One is a permanent desire, okay? This is basically the big three is health, wealth, and relationships, okay? These are desires that never leave us, okay? The mass population, all there, we all have a shared common desire of wanting to be healthy because obviously we want to live, wanting to obtain wealth because obviously we want to be able to experience life and we want to have great relationships, okay? We want to be able to be with, you know, we're social creatures, okay? So those three desires are the most dominant desires and every other little desire kind of trinkles down from there but they typically all point back up. One of the good examples that I like to give is the iPhone, okay? That actually taps into all three of these desires, okay? It helps with your health as there's, I mean depending on who you ask, but there's things that you can do to track and monitor your health on there, right? And then there's wealth, okay? The iPhone can help you network with people and can help you actually make money from your phone and there's relationships. Obviously that's the whole reason why the iPhone was created. It helps you actually connect with people, okay? So that's an example of why Apple and their main product is a trillion dollar company is because it goes to the extreme of all three of those desires and it's something that every single person wants. Now let's go down to trending desire. What is a trending desire? Well, a trending desire is things like crypto or like Valentine's Day and crypto, we'll see. AI, right? These are just examples of what trending desires have been right now and essentially these are desires that come and go, okay? There may be times where these trendy desires become permanent desires but for the most part these are trending desires, right? That, you know, 2021 kind of, you know, bull marketing crypto. Everybody was like crypto, crypto, crypto and then it started and then it, you know, came back down and now nobody was really talking about it anymore, right? At that time though, if you were selling Bitcoin t-shirts, you were probably doing pretty good. Valentine's Day, right? This is something that comes and goes, okay? Obviously every Friday or every Friday, every February, if you sell flowers, you probably see a massive spike on Valentine's Day or just before Valentine's Day. Why? Because there's a desire in the market to celebrate this kind of holiday. So that's an example of a trending desire and just know that we need to make sure that these, we understand both of these but most importantly the permanent desires are the ones that are going to give us the long-term results but trending desires are a great way to really drive short-term gain. Now, desire strength. Let's talk about essentially the strength of desire and why sometimes certain desires are, or certain businesses essentially are able to grow a lot further than some other businesses, okay? And essentially where your business, the amount of desire that your business can channel will determine how scalable your business is, at least that's what we've seen, okay? So the strength your desire will determine ultimately the success of your ad. So not just your business but now obviously your ads and your landing pages and everything else around it, okay? So basically your goal is to try to find the most dominant desire based on these two things. There's actually three so everything that I'm referencing I'll actually give you a resource at the end of this but essentially there's three things that determine the strength of your desire but I just tell people when you're first learning this stuff to just focus on two and that's essentially the intensity of the desire, okay? So like minor headache versus severe migraine, right? Like if I have a minor headache I'm like yeah whatever, right? But if I have a severe migraine I'm gonna be like I need to figure out how to get this gone, right? So the intensity of your desire will determine obviously the basically how dominant it is and then the second part of that is just the scope, okay? So the total amount of people that actually share this desire, okay? So we'll get into some examples of that as well but that is also going to determine how dominant the desire is. Are we talking about something that is mass mass market that everybody shares, right? Or is it just a very very nice small thing, okay? So for example here this airplane is your app, right? And the way that I like to help people understand this is essentially if you don't know this when you're actually flying there are sometimes like crosswinds, there's tailwinds and there's headwinds, okay? So basically a tailwind is I don't know if you've ever had a pilot come on the term or if you've never flown before you know this is what happens they'll come on the thing and say hey you know we were scheduled for you know three hours but looks like we got a bit of a tailwind with us so we should get there and about you know about two and a half or two and a quarter whatever it is, right? So the time for you to get there is significantly less because they're flying in a tailwind. So desire is kind of like this tailwind that basically gives you a boost. So you put your ad basically you put your plane up in the sky and essentially a tailwind what it will do is it will like almost jet rock or jet pack your your your ad and and let it do a lot better and that basically help you achieve your goals a lot faster. Excuse me, so that is a tailwind. BESTAND: 8 Evolve - What Is Identification Marketing.mp4
============================================================

All right, so in this next module, we're gonna be talking about identification, which is one of the most powerful forms of marketing that for all of my fashion brands, my accessory brands, my jewelry brands, this is going to be the module that helps you better understand, because for example, if you were going through the desire module and you're like, ah, you know, I don't really know if I have like a problem solution style ad that I can run, you know, for my black and green D-shirt, right? This is where identification marketing is going to come into play. Now, if you are not an accessory or fashion, or, you know, or jewelry brand or anything like that, you still need to watch this, because if you can tie desire marketing with identification marketing, basically use identification to amplify the desires, this is where you will start to really surpass all of your competition, because you're, as we're about to get into, painting the picture of who your customer desires to become. So for those of you who don't, have never heard of identification marketing or identity marketing, it's basically gonna dive deeper into the desire of what we as people want to kind of act out, you know, we buy things and we do things in certain ways for the way that we want to be seen by the world, okay? So it's basically, as it says there, how we choose to define ourselves to the world as a specific kind of person, okay? So it's not essentially the desire for satisfaction, so for example, if I have a migraine and I just wanna fix my migraine, that is obviously like I'm just trying to get that desire satisfied, whereas in most, in identification marketing, we are essentially trying to market how people want to be recognized and how people want to express themselves, okay? So identity marketing is about showcasing who your product helps your customer become or embrace who your customer already is, and identification marketing is essentially how we communicate feelings of customer desires without words, okay? So I'm gonna start this off with a little bit of a fun exercise just to give you a better idea and help you see in the real world how we basically symbolize identity.
